Chapter 20.
On the cauterization of teeth and the softening of gums.

Chapter 21.
On the cauterization of tooth pain.
When tooth pain is caused by coldness, or if there is a crack or worm in the tooth, and you do not achieve results with medicine, then cauterize it in two ways: either with a cow's udder cautery or with fire.
Cauterizing with a cow's udder involves taking a cow's udder and heating it in a fire until it is red hot. Then take a piece of iron or other metal, wrap it in cloth, and place it over the end of the heated tool. Next, immerse the tool in boiling water and quickly place it on the painful tooth until it becomes numb.
Then repeat this several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the teeth.
And if you wish, dip a piece of wool or cloth in the heated tool described above and place it on the painful tooth, holding the heated iron over it until it reaches the base of the concavity of the tooth.
However, cauterizing with fire involves paying attention to the size of the iron or copper tip and making sure it is large enough to cover the affected area without the heat of the flame reaching the patient's mouth.
And apply the heated cautery to the affected tooth, holding it with your hand until the cautery cools down; do this several times so that the pain may be alleviated either on that day or the following day.
And it is necessary that while the cautery is applied, the patient fills their mouth with good saliva and holds it there for an hour and then rinses their mouth; this is the method of using the cautery.
And cauterize any extremity that you can, as much as it is possible for you to do so.
And this is the form of the cannula (a tube used to drain fluid):

Then treat it with ointment and bandages until it is healed.

Chapter Twenty-Eight:
On Perforating Liver Abscess with Cautery:
When an abscess or swelling arises in the liver and you want to determine if it is located in the liver tissue itself or its outer membrane, then if it is in the liver tissue, the patient will experience heaviness and increased pain.
And if it is in the outer membrane of the liver, then the pain will be intense and sometimes even exhausting for doctors to treat.
Therefore, it is necessary to have the patient lie on their back with their head raised. However, even with experience, one should proceed with caution when performing this operation. But ultimately, it is up to your discretion and judgment.
Chapter Twenty-Nine:
On Cauterization of Plague Sores:
The ancients used to cauterize plague sores with rods made from the branches of Aristolochia plants in this way: take a dry rod about a finger's length from the branch of an Aristolochia plant, and make sure it is slender and pointed.

And it is not necessary to clamp your hand with the cautery, but rather hold it in an open position.
And some ancient men used to say that some people among them use a cautery of iron similar to a ray and burn that (place) with it, placing it in the location between the ribs until they reach that abscess and the pus is expelled, just as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with cautery there is not lack of fear, because one dies immediately if it happens in the location of a fistula where there is no healing.

Recipe for alkali and caustic lime, mixed in equal parts, grind them together and place the mixture in a new bowl with a small hole on the side that is just large enough to fit a finger through.

Galen speaks of a procedure and treatment for joint pain and sciatic nerve pain that was performed by an ancient physician, and he highly praises it, stating that no other treatment is necessary. He says that the patient was cured in one go, just as reported, and that the pain disappeared quickly after the treatment, leaving the patient free of discomfort. [Note: Galen was a prominent Greek physician who lived in the 2nd century AD.]
It is recommended to take green verdigris (a copper acetate compound), and if that is not available, fresh figs should be taken instead. These should be crushed together with a small amount of salt and applied as a poultice to the ankle, thigh, or leg where the pain is located, and then bandaged in place.
And it should be left in place for three hours or until the patient feels relief from the burning sensation.
Then place the affected area in warm water, and once the skin has turned red, expose it to the sun, for this will bring an end to the pain and promote healing.
And you should know that it is not necessary to use a cautery with these medicines, except in cases where there is need for the evacuation of bodily fluids (such as pus).
But Hippocrates says that when the vein is constricted due to a goat's horn wound, cauterization will be beneficial for the patient. The cautery should be applied in this manner: wool should be soaked in old oil and placed between the toes and under the arches of the feet.
Then take a dry goat's horn and heat it until it is charred, then place the charred horn on top of the wool and leave it in place until it has extended (i.e., until it cools and contracts, pulling on the skin). Then repeat this process until the sensation of biting has spread to the ankle and the pain is relieved.
This method of cauterization is called "cautery of cows." (Note: The name may refer to the use of a horn, which is a cow's horn.)

And then place the heated cautery on top of the clavus and rotate your hand with the cautery around the circumference of the wound until the cautery reaches the depth of the wound. Chapter LVI.
On the cauterization of a flow of blood caused by an accident through incision of an artery.
Many times a flow of blood occurs from an artery that is incised near the wound, either from outside or from incisions in abscesses or cauterization of a limb, and it is difficult to heal such a one.
Therefore, when this happens, you should immediately place your hand over the opening of the artery and press with your finger on the incision so as to obstruct the flow of blood from the wound until it stops.
And then place the olive-shaped cauteries, large and small in number, on the fire so that they become very hot. Then blow on them until they are red hot.
Then take one that is either small or large, depending on the location and the wound in which the artery has been severed. Place it quickly over the vein onto which you have placed your finger, and cauterize the area until it is seared and the blood flow stops.
And if the blood continues to flow from the opening of the artery as you lift your finger and remove the cautery, then quickly take another heated cautery from those that have been prepared in the fire, and do not stop doing this until the bleeding stops.
And be careful that you do not burn the nerves that are nearby, causing another injury to the patient.
And you should know that when blood flows from an artery, it is not possible to stop the bleeding in any other way than by one of four methods: either with a cautery as we have described, or through extraction if it has not already been extracted, because when it has been extracted the extremities are better able to heal and the bleeding is stopped. Or bind it tightly with a ligature of either gall or lime for strong compression. Or apply medicines to it that have the power to stop bleeding; they should be strengthened with a bolster and proper bandaging.
But those who administer proper compression through the use of lime and binding with cloth or by means of burning causes and similar methods should not be trusted.
But if this happens when the doctor is not present and there is no medicine available, then place your finger over the opening of the vein as we have described, and apply firm pressure until the bleeding stops at the top of the wound, without pressing on the artery. Then sprinkle cold water with great forcefulness onto the artery so that the blood congeals and thickens; and consider what kind of cautery or medicine is necessary.

Chapter 30: On the Extraction of Teeth.

On the extraction of abscesses from both ears and those that are located in the throat, as well as other abscesses.
When it happens in the throat, these are glands that become swollen and collect together like cotton, which when they appear outside are called tonsils (or two ears), and if you treat them with what we have said in the division and they do not heal, then you should consider if the abscess is hard, of dark color, and with little feeling, then you should not touch it with iron.
And if it is of red color and the surface is rough, then you should not touch it with iron because of the flow of blood; instead let it mature inside, and then either you will lance it or it will break open by itself.
And if it is of white color, soft and the surface is fine, then that is what should be incised.
And the operation in it is that you consider before your operation if the abscess has rested after being cauterized or has decreased in size; and then make the patient face the sun, their head near yours, hold their mouth open, and have a servant holding the tongue down with an elegant instrument of which this is the form:

And sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat, besides those two tonsils, and you should incise these in the same way as described for the two tonsils.
And I have treated a woman who had an abscess in her throat that was turning dark purple, with little sensation, and she had closed her own throat, and the woman was breathing with difficulty, and she had been forbidden to eat or drink water, and she would have died if it hadn't been for my intervention within one day or two.
And the abscess had grown so much that it had taken two months to burst through two openings.

And then I cut away a large portion of it and only a small amount of blood came out. And eventually, new abscesses formed in place of the old one, which I continued to lance until they were completely healed.
Therefore I inserted a probe and cauterized the woman's throat, so that was that; and then I walked around and didn't know what God had in store for me with her.

Chapter 39.
On the extraction of bloodletting attached to the gallbladder.
When you are medicating a bloodsucker with what we have said in the division of treatment with medicines and not with cautery, then look at the gallbladder of the patient in the sun, after you have compressed the tongue of the patient with the instrument that we have recommended to you.
Therefore, if you see the bloodsucker, extract it with a small lancet or fine forceps appropriately.
And if it is not possible for you to remove it with that, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the patient's gallbladder, place an iron instrument in the concavity of the cannula and do this several times (until the bloodsucker is dead and has separated from the gallbladder) and ensure that the patient abstains from water for the entire day.
And then take a full bladder of warm water and pour it into that, and rinse the area with it; and ensure that no other cause or illness enters that bladder, and let the patient drink the water an hour at a time with his hand, as the bloodsucker will soon be attracted to the water.
However, if it has not been expelled with what we recommended, then fumigate the patient with cinquefoil or asafoetida using the instrument that we recommended in the fumigation of the uvula.
Do this for four days.
And here is another way of operating in the fumigation of that location: take a pot with hot coals inside and cover it with a lid, in the middle of which there should be a hole, and fit the tip of the instrument into that hole; then perform the fumigation from above and place the patient's mouth on the end of the cannula and seal their mouth so that the fumigation does not escape until you are sure that the fumigation has reached the bloodsucker, as the bloodsucker will soon fall.
And if it does not fall, then you should repeat the fumigation several times, and ensure that the patient abstains from drinking water, and eat salty foods and garlic, and also necessary is that with this regimen it is expelled.
And this is the shape of the instrument with which to treat bloodsuckers in the gallbladder when it is visible, and it is similar to forceps, but with a slight curve. which should be placed in the gallbladder, and the end of it resembles a stork's beak, which is curved, with a file on it so that when compressing any cause, it does not let go.
Chapter 40.
In which is the essence of the sermon on abscesses and their section.
Abscesses are many species, in many ways, depending on what comes to mind, of each one in this book.
And they are diverse in penetration and section in two ways: one is due to the nature of the abscess itself, and the other is due to what we compress from the moisture.
And the second way is related to the location in which they occur, as an abscess that occurs in the head is different from an abscess that occurs in the buttocks, and an abscess that occurs in a fleshy part of the body is different from an abscess that occurs in a joint; and each one has its own treatment through surgery.
And there are some abscesses which should not be penetrated until the pus in them has matured or they have healed.
And there are other abscesses which should be incised when they are hard and not mature according to their due time, such as abscesses that are close to joints, for an abscess near a joint is prolonged until you can reach what is around it, and the ligaments or nerves of that joint are easily corrupted, causing contraction of that limb; or if the abscess is near a major organ, then delay the incision until it has matured, lest the penetration damage the organ; or if it is near the buttocks, then incise it before it matures; and it is not necessary to incise it deeply if digestion is incomplete, but only if it is close to the buttocks, so that you do not penetrate too deeply and cause a fistula or damage to the surrounding area that has not healed. But one must know the time of incision for an abscess, and that is when it has matured.
And you should know that it is mature when the pain has subsided and fever has ceased, and also when there is a decrease in redness and swelling, the hardness of the abscess has decreased, and other signs such as a change in color or the presence of pus. [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abscess#Signs\_and\_symptoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abscess#Signs_and_symptoms)
And it is necessary to know that the incision should be made below the abscess and in a place where pus can drain freely from the elevated part of the abscess. [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abscess#Incision\_and\_drainage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abscess#Incision_and_drainage)
And the incision should always be made along the length of the skin or body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the hands or feet, and on wrists, cords of nerves, arteries; and finally, in all places where there is no reflection, for in those that have reflection, use incision according to that member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy location, then it is better to leave the incision until digestion of the pus has been confirmed according to its due time, as we mentioned earlier; for if you penetrate it before that, the flesh will be torn and there will be much dirt, and the edges of the wound will become hardened and deep. [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abscess#Incision\_and\_drainage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abscess#Incision_and_drainage)
But some abscesses are penetrated according to the width of the skin or body, depending on necessity, or based on what part of the body requires it.
And it is necessary to perform a small incision for small abscesses and a large, wide incision or many sections according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses. [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abscess#Incision\_and\_drainage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abscess#Incision_and_drainage)
And there are other types of abscesses in which it is necessary for the incision to be concave and sutured when it has healed, such as those that occur in the groin or around the testicles (dubelec) and large pustules (bubos). [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bubo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bubo)
And of those that are incised with a section having three angles, there are those that are incised like the shape of a myrtle leaf, such as abscesses in the anus (angonars).
And of them there are those in which a round or crescent-shaped incision is made, similar to these.
But if there is one that does not have an abscess like a lion's claw (superficial abscess), then it is necessary to make a shallow or flat incision only.
And it is necessary when the abscess is large and has accumulated much pus, to penetrate it but not be afraid to drain all of the pus in that hour; after extracting a part of it, then fill the abscess again until the next day, and then extract a larger portion, and continue doing this gradually until it is fully drained.
And especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman in menstruation, or a small child, or an old person in decline, for the animal spirit is often dissolved by the egression of pus, and the patient may soon die if you do not operate on them. [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal\_spirit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_spirit)
Beware this chapter with great caution, and direct your penetration into the incision where you lance these abscesses; it is necessary that you clean the wounds and consider whether the abscess wound is small or a flat section; therefore, you should administer some of honey or vinegar; and if the abscess is large, and the cracks of the incision are many, it is necessary that you place a wick in each hole that join together.
And if a portion of the skin is separated or sunken in the circumference of the abscess, it is necessary that you close it with an old piece of cloth or thread made from wool, just like when you sew up bread or clothes, without moisture; and strengthen it within the third day; and then proceed to heal and care for it with appropriate ointments until it is healed.
But if you encounter bleeding during your operation, it is necessary that you administer warm water and wine in which a cloth has been soaked, and place it over the area of the blood flow many times.
But if the bleeding persists, it is necessary that you administer regulation and care and powders which I have recommended in many places of this our book and division.
But if it is in winter, and the area of the abscess has many nerves, it is necessary that you fill up with powders made from wine and warm oil, and place them on the areas.
And if it is in summer, and the areas are fleshy, it is necessary that you place powders made from water and oil or wine and oil, and everything should be warmed until the third day, as we have said; and then it is necessary that you release the abscess and clean it and administer appropriate care for it until it is healed.
And this is what is necessary for the understanding of the cure for abscesses in general, but according to the method of distinction I have already mentioned, each type of abscess requires a different method of care, as described in separate chapters.

Chapter 42.
Of the cutting out of scrofulas which occur in the neck.
Often, these abscesses occur in the neck, armpits, and groin; and sometimes they happen in other parts of the body.
And those that occur in the neck are many that are generated between the skin and flesh, and every scrofula of these is inside its own membrane, just as with nodes and abscesses of the head, as we have said before.
And the types of these scrofulas are many: some are hard like stone, and others contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that do not respond to treatment.
Therefore in the one that you see in good condition during touch, of which the color of the exterior is close to the color of the skin and is healthy all around, not attached to the neck nerve, veins, or arteries, and not prominent, it is necessary that you incise it with a dry surface from the upper part to the lower part of the body along the line of G to the line of B, and remove its entire exterior in this way, and stretch the two lips of the wound with one ounce or several ounces if necessary, as we have said in the abscesses of the head, and extract it little by little.
And there is need for more caution that the vein or nerve not be incised.
And the scalpel should not be too sharp so that it does not cause your hand to slip during incision, or disturb the patient, and that you do not incise what is unnecessary; because if you were to incise a vein or artery, it would prevent you from continuing in your operation. In this case, pause on the wound with vitriol trissat or other powders that stop bleeding, tighten the wound, and leave it until the acuteness of the abscess has subsided, the wound has softened and begun to become gangrenous. When the blood is cut off.
Therefore, return to your operation until you have completed it.
Then ask with your skilled judgement if there is any other small cause of the other scrofulas, and if so, incise those and clean them out.
And if the large vein is at the root of a large scrofula, it is necessary to not incise that scrofula from its root. Beforehand, it is better to bind the wound with doubled gall and leave it until it falls off by itself without causing harm.
Then fill the wound with old cotton that you have already soaked in Egyptian ointment, and take care of it.
And if you incise the entire scrofula, it is necessary to bring the two lips of the wound together and suture them as soon as possible so that there is no remaining excess.
But if you see that there is remaining excess due to the size of the scrofula, it is necessary to consider incising its root and drawing out that and administering suture in this way.
And for the scrofulas that contain moisture, make an incision with a superficial puncture in the place where you see maturation, and apply a puncture wound in the lower part of the body, as we have said before.
Then administer puncture, cauterization with ointment and similar methods so that it corrodes what is left of the corruption. And when you see that the wound is already cleaned, it is necessary to take care of it with flesh-generating ointment until it heals.

Of the cutting out of the pustule in the glands under the armpits. [Continued in next message...]
The ancients recommended this procedure for the pustule, but I have not seen anyone in our land perform it. [Continued in next message...](The rest of the text was not provided)

And for this reason, I command that the wound be left open until the evil of the illness has been consumed, and the evil of it lasts for three days; and then, therefore, I command to treat the wound in this way, and take care of it until it heals.
And what I have seen in my practice is that a maidservant took a knife and inserted it into her armpit, cutting a part of the lung's rib with it, and I was called to treat her wound, and I found the sound just like the mooing of the dead, and I discovered the wound and saw blood coming out of it in small amounts.

And the maidservant did not suffer any harm except for a change in her voice, and after several days she returned to normal health.
And now I say that there is no fear in cutting out the pustule.

Chapter 49.
On the incision of abscesses that occur due to arteries or veins.
When an artery is ruptured and the fascia (codena) above it has hardened, then many abscesses often occur. And the signs that indicate that inflammation and abscess are due to an artery or vein are: when the abscess is caused by an artery, it is elongated and located near the pulse of the body; and if you press on the abscess with your fingers, you will feel a stridor (a harsh grating sound) in it.
And when it is due to a vein, it is round and visible on the surface of the body. [Original text: "e aquel que es per vena es redon al manifest del cors."]
Incision of this type of abscess is dangerous, especially when it occurs in areas such as the armpits, groins, neck, and other parts of the body; and if it is very large, then surgical treatment with a knife should be avoided. Additionally, incisions on the extremities or head are also to be avoided.
But for an abscess caused by inflammation of the orifice (opening) of the artery, make an incision in the fascia along its length; and then use forceps to open up the incision and expose the artery, removing any sheaths that cover it.
And then place a needle over it and make the needle penetrate into the other side, and tightly tie the artery with double-stranded thread in two places - which is necessary for the extraction of two arteries that are present in temples (templars).
And then place your finger on the location between two ligaments with a spatula, allowing all of the blood in it to drain out and causing the abscess to be resolved.
And then apply treatment to the area where there is difficulty in movement due to swelling, until the ligaments are no longer taut; and apply appropriate ointments to it until it heals.
If the abscess is due to a ruptured vein, then place your hand as close as possible to the abscess along with the fascia; and then insert the needle under the location where you have placed your hand, making it penetrate; and tie it in double thread until you extract it from the other side, and bind the abscess with a ligament as I mentioned before using two parts of the thread with two extremities.
But if you are afraid of extracting the thread, then insert it with a needle all around the abscess before making the initial incision, and tightly tie your threads in four places.
And then make an incision in the middle of the abscess until all that is contained within it comes out; after which, cut away any excess fascia and leave what remains attached to it alone.
And then place a soft cloth soaked in wine and oil over it; and apply the treatment consisting of compresses and ointments until it heals.
Chapter 51: On abscesses that occur due to nerve twisting.
Just as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, similarily abscesses can also occur in nerves when there is a blow or excessive work, and due to other reasons.
The majority of these abscesses occur in the locations of tendons or at the heel, or in any location where joints are under pressure.
This abscess is serious and similar in color to other parts of the body; it occurs on the back or side of the limb and when compressed with force, the patient appears to be in a state of stupor.
This abscess is not elongated along the pulse of the body and is located below the fascia; it is harmful to all parts of the limb and does not spread towards the front or back.
Therefore for those abscesses that occur in joints, it is not advisable to make incisions with a knife, as this can easily lead to contracture (a condition in which the muscles or tendons become permanently shortened and thickened).
However, for those abscesses that occur on the head or forehead, make an incision in the fascia using a surgical tool like a spatula. But if it is a small abscess, then use forceps and cut it with precision.
If it is large, then suspend it with forceps and remove the surrounding tissue; apply dressing to it and close the wound using stitches; and treat it until it heals.

On incisions for abscesses that occur in the lower abdomen, near the navel.
Many men often develop abscesses in their lower abdomens or other parts of their bodies that resemble mushrooms due to their subtle roots and large caps; the lips surrounding them are already converted (infected), and they can be small or very large.
I have seen one such case where two abscesses in the lower abdomen closely resembled mushrooms; they were white and had fine roots.
And the lips around them were turned inside out and splitting open, with fluid constantly oozing from it.
Therefore I incised these abscesses and found one to be very heavy, weighing 18 ounces (unc). And the other one weighed 5 ounces (vi unc).
And the operation for incising these abscesses requires you to consider whether the patient is moist and their skin is white, soft, with fine roots; if so, then make an incision using a broad spatula and have cauteries ready in the fire, as much blood will flow from the incision and you must cauterize it if necessary.
If the patient is weak and fearful, be careful not to incise with a knife; instead, take fresh lead filings and tie them to the skin using the method mentioned earlier; then leave it for two days.
And then tighten the lead filings in the stricture; do not stop tightening the large amount of lead until it is cut and falls off by itself without any effort on your part.
But if the abscess is large and there is a reason to be afraid or anxious, especially when it occurs in the lower abdomen.
But it is also possible that you make an incision in the abscess and then cauterize it to prevent it from returning.
And then treat it until the wound heals completely.

Chapter 52: On treating abscesses caused by blows or wounds to the body.
Treatment for a protrusion (eminence) of the navel.
A protrusion (eminence) of the navel can be caused by many reasons, including: a rupture in the membrane or fascia that covers the abdomen, causing tissue or hernia to bulge out; bleeding from a vein or artery; or trapped gas in the intestines. [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical\_hernia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical_hernia)
But if it is due to a rupture of the membrane and herniation of tissue, then the abscess will be similar in color to the surrounding skin; it may not cause pain, and its appearance can vary depending on the size and location of the protrusion. If it is due to herniation of the bowel, then its location will depend on the reason for the protrusion, with much greater variation in appearance; when pressed with your fingers, it will temporarily disappear and then return quickly; it can be easily pushed back in, but may become larger during physical exertion or bathing.
But if it is due to trapped fluid, then it will not be painful and will not disappear when pressed with the hand; it also will not be constricted or enlarged.
If it is due to bleeding, then the abscess will appear dark and purple-black in color.
But if it is due to fatty tissue, then the abscess will be large and firm with a fixed size.
And if it is due to trapped gas, then touching it will feel soft.
And the operation for treating a protrusion of the navel requires you to consider whether it is caused by bleeding from an artery or vein, or trapped gas; if so, then it is best to avoid treatment as there is a risk of serious complications as mentioned in the chapter on abscesses caused by arteries and veins. [Reference(s):](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical_hernia)
But if the protrusion of the navel is caused by herniation of tissue or membrane, then you should instruct the patient to lie on their back with legs extended; and then use a probe to examine the entire navel area and mark the location of the protrusion; next, have the patient turn over onto their stomach with their hips between your hands, and then use a broad spatula to make an incision along the circumference of the navel around the marked location; and then extend the herniated tissue outwards using large forceps, and tie it in place with strong or loose thread as appropriate. [Reference(s):](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical_hernia)
And then place the middle of the protrusion over the ligament and insert your finger into it to feel for the herniated bowel; if you find it, then hold onto it carefully and gently push it back inside the abdominal cavity.
If you find tissue instead, then use forceps to grasp it and make an incision to remove any excess tissue. [Reference(s):](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical_hernia)
But if the incision is near an artery or vein, then carefully tie it off with thread and return to your operation; then take two needles and tie them with strong threads, inserting them into the circumference of the incision in a cross shape; and then tightly bind the abscess in four parts along the needles. [Reference(s):](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical_hernia)
If you prefer, remove the needles and leave the area open so that it can heal on its own; or when the wound has closed slightly, make an incision along the edges to allow for better healing, then treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals completely. [Reference(s):](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical_hernia)
And if the prominence of the navel is due to flesh or moisture, then it is necessary for you to evacuate the abscess as we have said, extract the blood or moisture that you find in it, and then heal and solidify the area with whatever is appropriate.
Chapter 53.[*](https://ell.stackexchange.com/questions/312460/the-following-text-is-a-medieval-medical-treatise-written-in-a-language-th#fn:1)
On the treatment of cancer.[*](https://ell.stackexchange.com/questions/312460/the-following-text-is-a-medieval-medical-treatise-written-in-a-language-th#fn:2)
We have said, in the discussion, of the type of cancer and in what manner it is treatable with medicine, and that it is advisable to treat it with surgery so that it does not become ulcerated; and we have said cancer generated in the mother's womb and carefulness in the treatment of it.
And the ancients said that sometimes cancer is in a location where it is possible to eradicate it, such as a crab that is in the breasts or in the groin and similar locations on the limbs that can be completely removed, and especially when it is beginning and small.
But when it is advanced and large, it is not advisable to attempt to treat it, because it cannot be cured, nor have I seen or heard of anyone who has been cured, or that such a thing has occurred.
And the operation for it, when it is located as we have said, is that you proceed and let the patient undergo purging of black bile several times, and bleed them if there is clear congestion.
And prepare the patient with preparation in which they are located for the operation, and prohibit them from consuming any food or drink; and make sure that the surgical instruments, such as forceps, are ready; and ensure that the cavity is completely clean and free of any remaining causes of the roots of it. And let the blood flow and do not cut it lightly, but press on the areas and wipe away the thick blood with your hand or with an instrument that is within your reach among the surgical tools.
But if there is opposition to the flow of thick blood from a vein or artery, then cauterize it until the bleeding stops and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
Chapter 50.
On the treatment of hydropsy (dropsy).
We have already mentioned, in the discussion, the types of hydropsy and their symptoms, and the treatment with medicine.
And the type of hydropsy that can be cured with surgery is only the type of ascites (abdominal fluid accumulation), and it is not advisable to use surgery for the types of tympanites (distention of the abdomen) or hypochondrium (pain in the lower abdomen), because that is fatal.
And when you have treated this type of hydropsy, tympanites, with medicine and it does not respond to your treatment, then consider, because if the patient has already become weakened or is suffering from another illness or hydropsy in addition, such as cough or abdominal pain, etc., then be cautious and do not treat them with surgery, because there is danger in doing so.
But if you see that the patient has robust vitality, and is suffering only from hydropsy without any other illness, and they are neither infants nor elderly, then the method of surgery for them is to lift the patient between your hands, place a basin under their belly, make them expel the air in their stomach with their hand, press on the lower part of the abdomen, and take a sponge as follows:
should be long with two sharp ends like a sponge, but it should have some shortness to it gradually, so that during the operation you do not penetrate the intestines and damage them.
And also consider whether the cause of hydropsy is from the intestines, because in that case you must make an incision away from the navel by three fingers' width towards the lower abdomen, to the right of it.
But if the cause of hydropsy is due to liver disease, then your incision should be to the left of the navel by three fingers' width.
And if the cause of hydropsy is due to the spleen, then your incision should be on the right side.
And it is not advisable to make your incision on the side where the patient will lie, because that could cause fluid accumulation in that location.
And also penetrate the entire thickness of the abdominal wall with your instrument, enter that incision and lift your hand with the spatula between the abdominal wall and the peritoneum (the membrane lining the abdominal cavity), and scrape it off; and remove a quantity equivalent to a fingernail or thereabouts.
And also penetrate the omentum (fatty tissue in the abdomen) until you reach the empty space and the location of the fluid. And then remove it and insert an instrument with this shape: and it resembles a thin silver cannula, made of silver or copper or lead, with a small hole at the lowest part of it, and on both sides there are three holes: two on one side and one on the other, and its tip is sharpened like a feather quill, as you can see:
And at the top of it is an armilla (a ring-shaped device), because when the instrument reaches the fluid, it quickly fills up with water and then evacuates it in half the quantity, as if you remove too much water in one go, it can cause the patient to die from loss of vital spirits or lead to symptoms that are indicative of imminent death.
But you should evacuate it according to the patient's vitality and based on your observations of their condition, including the strength of their pulse and overall health status.
And then remove the instrument and retain the water that has accumulated, which is caused by the abdominal wall retaining it through the hole in the omentum that you were advised to make earlier.
And then repeat the procedure with the instrument on the following day if you see that the patient can tolerate it, and extract a small amount of fluid, and do this for several days out of caution, but make sure not to leave too much fluid behind.
But if you are concerned about the patient's condition and have left behind a large amount of fluid, then treat them with hot sand packing and mustard plasters in a bath, and expose them to the sun for a long time, and treat them with drying medicines until they are healed.
And use cautery on the stomach, liver and spleen during fluid removal, as I have mentioned earlier in what has been said before.
Chapter 55.
On the treatment of newborn infants with non-perforated urethral openings.
Sometimes, some newborns are born from their mother's womb with the head of their umbilical cord not pierced (or it is pierced narrowly or not in its proper place).
Therefore, it is necessary to cut the umbilical cord with a piercing (using a very thin spatula) in the following way as soon as the baby is born:
And then insert a thin nail made of lead into the piercing and tie it (to the umbilical cord), leaving it in place for three days or four.
And when the child wants to urinate, help them do so and then return (the nail) back into its place.
And if you don't insert the lead nail, it is possible that the urine flowing over the area will not be able to flow properly.
But for the one with a narrow piercing (in their umbilical cord), they should be treated with a lead nail as I have said, for many days until it becomes wider.
But for those in whom the piercing is not in its proper place, it is serious, as this causes a problem, because for some newborns, their umbilical cord is too long and they are born with the piercing at the end of the penis, preventing them from urinating properly. They must raise their penis with their hand to allow the urine to flow until the cord shortens on its own; this is not harmful to the newborn, but it is serious because the semen cannot reach the mother as it should, leading to a prolonged illness.
The method of the operation is as follows: place the patient on their back and extend the head of their penis with your left hand using strong traction, inserting the tip of the glans into the piercing using a sharp instrument like a feather quill or scalpel, without cutting any part, so that the urethral meatus aligns with the head of the penis and the piercing falls in its proper place as it should be.
And be careful during your operation to avoid causing any blood flow, as this often happens. Place a cloth at the site of incision to absorb any bleeding and treat the wound until it heals completely.

Of albugo, which occurs in the foreskin at the head of the penis, and of corruption, blackening, and adhesion of the foreskin to the head of the penis.

Because caustics can be used in two ways at the same time, either to stop bleeding or to treat a corrupted wound.

In the case of adhesion of the foreskin to the head of the penis (which does not occur unless the foreskin is healthy and uncircumcised, but may occur due to injury or abscess), it is necessary to perform a blunt dissection with a scalpel until the ligaments are dissolved and the glans are completely freed.
If it is difficult to separate the adhered foreskin from the head of the penis carefully, then it is necessary to perform a blunt dissection with a scalpel on both the glans and the foreskin. This is because the foreskin, when thin, can easily be pierced due to its delicate nature.

Chapter 57.
Of the purification of infants and the treatment of issues that arise from circumcision.
Circumcision is not like other wounds or injuries in that it is an intentional act, and the care of infants after this procedure requires special attention. Therefore, it is necessary to assign the best method and lightest approach to ensure their health.
Therefore, I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their free men because it was not part of their laws. However, we have learned through experience that circumcision is beneficial for infants. This is why most surgeons and barbers use a scalpel or razor for circumcision and ligation with thread and incisions using nails.
I have tried all of these methods and have found that using forceps is the best method for purification because it avoids cutting too deep into the foreskin, which has two layers. Only the outer layer is removed, leaving the inner layer intact and reducing pain and discomfort. And the digital method of purification performed by mohels is not safe because it is easy for them to insert the instrument too deep into the urethra, causing injury or infection.
However, using a nail in the operation can easily cause damage and corrupt your work. And the foreskin of infants is naturally short, and many times it does not require circumcision. I have seen this myself.
But through experience, I have found that circumcision using forceps and ligatures with suture is the best method because the forceps are designed for proportional incision, meaning the sharpness of the instrument above matches the sharpness below. This allows for precise cutting as you apply pressure evenly on both sides, ensuring a clean cut without error. Additionally, using suture creates compression that covers the entire foreskin, further reducing the risk of complications.
The first method of operation is to place the infant in a comfortable position, and then apply the ligature around the foreskin without cutting it. This should be left in place for one day before proceeding with the next step.
Then, do your best to comfort and soothe the child throughout the procedure, using gentle words and gestures that help them feel at ease. Also, make sure the child is securely positioned and not moving during the procedure. You can hide the forceps in your hand or under a cloth so that the child does not see them or any of the other instruments used.
Then, gently place your hand on the child's penis and blow on the foreskin to relax it. Slowly pull back the foreskin until the glans is exposed. Use a clean cloth or gauze to remove any smegma or dirt that has accumulated underneath the foreskin. [*]  E de aquo que accideys en le operacio, si es perforat o corrot le cap de la vergua, lahoras cove que tu cauterices aquel amb cauteri lunar; e s’es cremat o malaut, lahoras cura aquel am enguent asech.
Here is the shape of the forceps used for circumcision:
The ends of the forceps should be blunt and not sharp, with only one side having a cutting edge that does not exceed the width of the blade. Both sides of the forceps should be equal in length, similar to the size of two handles.
However, a common mistake in circumcision is to accidentally cut the inner foreskin or a portion of it instead of the outer layer.
Therefore, you should first pull back the inner foreskin with your finger before making the incision, to ensure that only the outer layer is cut evenly and accurately.
If you cannot hold it with your finger, then use a hemostat to pull back the inner foreskin and make the incision carefully.
But if three days have passed and the swelling has not subsided, then leave it alone for a few more days until the swelling goes down on its own. Then carefully dissect the remaining tissue and make the incision as prepared.
And be careful not to cut the glans, as it could harm the infant.
Therefore, treat the wound with a powder that promotes healing, as recommended in the section on powders in this treatise.
If the foreskin is cut too short and exposes the glans, it is not harmful to the infant.
And continue to care for the wound as previously recommended until it heals completely.
Chapter 58.
Treatment for urinary retention in the bladder.
Urinary retention in the bladder can be caused by obstruction due to a stone or coagulated blood, pus or flesh, and similar causes as mentioned in the previous section on methods of treatment.
If the stone is not dissolved with the previously mentioned methods and becomes a serious problem for the patient, then it is necessary to extract it using an instrument called a syringe, which has this shape: It should be made of silver, thin and concave like a bird's quill with a length similar to a palm and a half, with a thin cannula at the tip. [*]  E aprop conponeys le siringua sobre la peyra e trahys aquela am gentil traicio entro que sia dissolta en lo sieu loc; e si no es dissoluda, lahoras cove que tu la extirpes per aquella via.
The method of extracting urine with the syringe is to take double-folded thread or cloth and tie it tightly around the tip of the instrument. Insert the ends of the thread into the lower part of the syringe, and use forceps to remove any excess threads that may interfere. Then, insert the cannula into the urethra with firmness. Finally, gently pull on the syringe while applying pressure with a piece of egg white or albumen to help extract the stone.
And place the patient on a couch, puncture the bladder and urethra with oiled (medical) instruments, using olive oil and water.
Then introduce the catheter with ease until it reaches the tip of the urethra; then bend the penis upwards at its base and push the catheter further inside; ensure that it enters the bladder completely, allowing the patient to urinate and empty their bladder. This should be done in order, but if there's a deviation causing tortuosity, proceed accordingly.
Then gradually extract the bile using soft wool, as the wool absorbs the urine.
Then extract it (the stone) and perform a cure using the catheter without stopping, until the bladder is emptied and the patient feels relief.
Chapter 59.
On the quality of bladder irrigation using a clamp-like device and similar instruments that are suitable for this purpose.
When there is an ulceration or abscess in the bladder, or coagulated blood within it, or if the urethra is narrowed, and you wish to irrigate the area with water and medicine, then use an instrument known as a clamp-like device, which has this form:
...but its exterior is closed (blocked). And in it, there are three openings: two on one side, allowing for urination.
At the beginning, there is a concave space that holds (retains) what is inserted into it, and its size corresponds to the amount that is placed inside; when any force is applied on the fluids within, causing them to be drawn out, they should be expelled in this manner. When they are expelled forcibly, they will be pulled out with this process, similar to how a clamp-like device operates, such as one used to spray naptha during naval battles.
Therefore, if you wish to prevent fluids from entering the bladder, insert the end of the clamp into the fluid and draw it upwards towards the openings above, as the fluid will be drawn into the concavity of the clamp.
Then insert the end of the clamp into the urethra as previously recommended for the catheter; and push the fluid upwards, causing it to reach the bladder quickly, allowing the patient to urinate.
The subtle form of the catheter that is used to irrigate the bladder is as follows:
The catheter should be made of silver or lead, with the tip resembling a small feather; and it tapers downwards as it extends in length.
Then take the bladder in motion, place inside it the liquid you wish to irrigate with, and secure it between two objects using a strong ligature with double bile; then heat the liquid over a fire.
Then insert the end of the catheter into the urethra.
Then firmly press your hand over the bladder with the liquid, applying gentle pressure until the patient feels that the liquid has entered the bladder.

Then fill it with what you want from the liquids, such as oil and water.
Then attach the funnel to the device and proceed as you did with the bladder, expressing the liquid into it using your hand until it reaches the bladder.
Chapter 60.
On the Extraction of Stones.
We have already discussed in the division of stones and their cures using medicines, as well as the difference between stones generated in the kidneys and those generated in the bladder, along with signs indicating their presence.
And we have said that stones can be operated on using a hand and a scalpel.
And the stone generated in the bladder properly speaking is that which is lodged in the bladder.
I will now describe this with clear and concise explanation.
I say that the stone generated in the bladder mainly affects children; and its signs are: the urine that flows from the bladder resembles water in its subtlety, appearing as sand in it; the patient rubs their urethra and experiences frequent pain, which is sometimes severe; and they have difficulty sitting down due to discomfort.
And the healing of children with this condition occurs before they reach 14 years old, but it is difficult to cure in the elderly. But in young people, it is easier due to their age and vitality.
And for the person with a larger stone, the cure is more difficult; and if there are few (stones), it is contrary to this.
Therefore, when we come to the cure of this condition, it is necessary at the beginning that the patient be cleaned using an enema that extracts all the folds in their intestines, as these folds sometimes prevent the removal of the stone due to its location.
Then the patient should lie on their back with their feet elevated and massaged to encourage the stone to move towards the bottom of the bladder or dislodge from its current position.
Then perform the massage with your hands, preparing them in advance, and have the patient lie down on their back with their legs apart, allowing the bladder to tilt towards the lower part of the body.
Then search for the stone and extract it completely.
Therefore, if you feel the stone in the area, cut into it immediately with a scalpel.
And if you cannot feel the stone completely, then it is necessary to anoint your left index finger with oil and insert it into the patient's rectum. If the patient is a child, use the entire finger; or if they are an adult, use only half of it. Then search for the stone with your finger until you feel its presence at the tip. And gradually move your finger towards the neck of the bladder, feeling the path as you go.
Then press on the stone with your finger and gently push it out of the bladder through the incision you made earlier.
And instruct the assistant to press on the bladder with their hand; and instruct another assistant to use one hand to extend the patient's legs upwards, while using their other hand to support the lower back, just below the incision site.
Then insert a sharp spatula of this form: And make an incision in the area between the patient's rectum and legs, not too close to the anus, but rather towards the left hip bone; the incision should be made over the stone, with your finger inside the rectum, creating a transverse cut that is wider on the outside and narrower on the inside, according to the size of the stone. Make the incision as small as possible while still allowing for easy removal of the stone; this will minimize compression of the finger holding the stone during extraction.
And know that some stones have an angle and edges, making it difficult for urine to pass from them.
And that one resembles a lion's glans (or acorn) in shape, and is round, and is made of relatively easy-to-urinate material.
Therefore, if it is one with angles and edges, adjust it in the fissure.
And if it is not easily adjustable, then you should engrave on that one, or apply force to it appropriately, with the end of the instrument being like a file with which you apply force to the stone, and do not avoid contact with it; or insert a thin instrument with a curved tip under it.
But if you cannot get on top of it, then widen the hole slightly, and if you want blood flow, cut it strongly with three times heated vitriol.
But if the stone is larger than one, then at the beginning you should push your hand to the bladder opening and make an incision on it; and similarly, you should push slightly on it; and do the same if there are more than two.
And if the stone is very large, then know that you should not make an incision on it with a wide section, because this may cause two things to happen to the patient: either they will die or they will develop continuous urine leakage, because the area is not completely healed.
But administer an expulsion of it while it is being removed, or use forceps to extract it through the crack until it comes out in pieces.
And when you have completed your operation, then fill the wound with aloe and dragon's blood, and strengthen it. And place a cloth soaked in oil and vinegar, or rose oil and water, on top of it, so that the abscess may soften.
And then lay the patient on their side, and do not loosen the ligament until the third day.
And when you have loosened it, moisten the area with water and some oil, and treat the wound with fine ointment and zinc ointment until it is healed.
But if an abscess occurs in the wound that is painful and corrosive, and it resembles something like blood clots in the bladder that prevent urination (and this is known by the expulsion of blood with urine), then insert your finger into the wound and remove the blood clot, because if it remains it can cause corruption of the bladder and putrefaction.
And then wash the wound with sour vinegar, water and salt, and use any other remedy that is appropriate for it until it is healed.
And during the entire treatment, it is necessary that you lie down with your thighs apart and adjust the medications that are placed on the area.
And if the stone is small and located in the meat of the penis, and has become embedded in it, and urination is prohibited, then treat it with what I recommended before reaching incision, because many people have been accused of causing injury through this treatment; and it is true and proven that you should use a soft iron perforator, which looks like this:
with a triangular point, sharp, inserted into a handle.
And then take bile, and tie it to the penis below the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
And then insert the iron into the penis, perforating easily until it reaches the stone. And rotate the perforator with your hand in that stone little by little, and you will widen the hole until you make it penetrate from the other side; because urination will be released immediately.
And then press your hand on what remains of the stone from the side that is outside the penis, because it is trapped and has been removed with the urine, and the patient is healed.
But if this treatment is not available to you for any reason that prevents it, then tie a bile below the stone, and another one above the stone. And then cut into the stone in the penis between two ligatures. And then extract it. And then loosen the ligature and clean up the clotted blood, which is done in the wound.
And it is not necessary to use a ligature of bile below the stone, but only to prevent it from returning to the bladder, and the other ligature above it should not be used, because when the bile is loosened, the expulsion of the stone occurs, the kidney returns to its place and heals the wound.
And so it is necessary for you to raise the kidney when you tie the bile above it, or to return it to its place after completion, and heal the wound as we have said.
Capital LXI
On the Extraction of Stones from Women
Stones in women are rarely generated.
But if a stone is found in any of them, then the cure for it is difficult and is prevented by many methods.
One of the reasons is that women are easily frightened.
And the second reason is that you do not find a woman who is knowledgeable enough to reveal if she has allowed access to a doctor when she is chaste, or among women who have husbands.
And the third reason is that you do not find a woman who is knowledgeable in this art, especially the operation with hands.
And the fourth reason is that in women, the location of the incision for stones is far from the location of the stone itself, so a deeper incision is needed, and this carries fear.
But if necessity requires it, then you should take a knowledgeable woman as your assistant, but they are rarely found.
But if you are deprived of that, then look for an intelligent and skillful midwife, or present a mature woman who is knowledgeable in the matters of women, or a woman who has already been trained in this art.
Therefore, make that presentation and command her to do everything that you order, starting with the inquiry about the stone; which is necessary for her to check if the woman is a virgin, in which case she should insert her finger into the anus of the patient and feel for the stone.
Therefore, if she finds it, then press down on it with her finger and then command her to make an incision over it.
But if she is not a virgin, then command the midwife to insert her finger into the vagina of the patient and feel for the stone, while placing her left hand on the bladder and carefully examining it.
Therefore, if she finds it, then it is necessary to gradually move the stone from the orifice of the bladder towards the backside with increasing pressure until it reaches the crease of the thigh.
And approach and make an incision above the affected area of the leg, so that the razor is parallel to the thigh, place the stone on that part, and let the said stone not be constricting below it.
And the incision should be small at first; then introduce the razor into that incision and if you feel the stone, then adjust the depth of the incision according to the size you know the stone will require from it.
And know that the types of stones are many: for some are small and large, and rough, and elongated and round, and some have protrusions.
Therefore, you should know the type of stone present in the body to determine what you want to do about it.
And if you want to cause bleeding, apply vinegar of three times strength in the area and leave it there for an hour until the blood flows, then return to your operation until the stone is removed.
And make sure to prepare the necessary instruments for the removal of stones in men, so that you are assisted by those tools during your operation.
And if you want to cause bleeding and know that the incision is on the artery, then place powder on the area and tighten it with a bandage and restrictive dressing, do not repeat this; and leave the stone alone and do not extract it, for the patient will die very soon. And take care of the wound.
And when the intensity of bleeding has subsided after several days and the area is healed, then return to your operation until the stone is removed.
Chapter 62. (This seems to be a heading or a new topic in the treatise)
On incision for inguinal hernia.
An inguinal hernia is nothing but an accumulation of fluid in the white membrane located behind the abdomen, which contains the water and is below the groin; it is called a "ciphac".
And sometimes it is in the same scrotum, which nature has prepared as a pouch for the water in that area, until it matures into another water; and this is the groin of the genitals between the white membrane we mentioned earlier, and this is nothing but fat.
And the cause of this hernia is due to weakness that occurs in the genitals, causing this matter to be infused into them, and sometimes it is caused by a blow to the genitals.
And this fluid has many colors, for its color may be tending towards yellow or red, or red, or black and fecal-like, or watery white, and that is the most common.
And the signs by which it is known where this accumulation of water is located are as follows: if it is in the white membrane we mentioned earlier, then a swelling will be round and slightly elongated, shaped like an egg, and the genitals will appear because the fluid surrounds them from all sides.
And if the fluid is in the scrotum itself, then the swelling will be round with an egg-like shape and because of this, it is thought to be another water.
And if the fluid is between the groin of the genitals and the white membrane, then a lump will be felt in that area.
And if you want to determine the color of the fluid, then press on the swelling with your fingers and observe the mark left behind; and based on the color that appears in the imprint, judge what it looks like inside.
Therefore, when we come to the treatment of this condition with iron (cauterization), it is necessary to order the patient to undergo venesection if it is possible for you, and bleed his body.
And turn him onto his stomach with a slight elevation under the waist, and place some cloth underneath him.
And you should position yourself on the left side of the patient, and order the assistant to stand at his right, extending his penis towards one of two sides, either towards the groin of the genitals or towards the navel.
And take a broad spatula and make an incision in the groin of the genitals from one end to near the pubic bone.
And make the incision following a straight line parallel to the skin of the genitals, until it reaches the white membrane and encompasses it.
And remove the membrane, observe and be careful not to cut through it; and make the incision in such a way that when you remove the membrane, it is suspended with the water sac, and examine carefully and as much as possible, the membrane you have removed.
And then puncture the white membrane filled with water with a wide incision and extract all the water.
And then separate the two lips of the incision with forceps and extend the white membrane towards both sides; do not touch the groin of the genitals, and cut the white membrane in such a way that it is possible for you to do so. And cut the white membrane entirely or in pieces, and especially its side that is towards you; for if you do not carefully examine the incision of it, there will be no certainty that the water does not return.
But if the water protrudes from the outside of its groin during your operation, then after you have completed the incision of the white membrane, return it inside, and then suture the two lips of the groin with stitches; and take care of it as you would for other wounds, until it is healed.
And if you find the water corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie the vessels that are above the suspending ligament, extract the water and take care of it as we mentioned before.
But if the water is collected in two areas, then know that there are two hernias; therefore incise the second part in the same way as you did with the first one. And if it seems to you that it is a single operation, then do it.
And then clean the blood, and insert into the incisions wool soaked in oil or rose oil; and place outside another wool that you have soaked in vinegar and oil, and spread it over both genitals and the navel; and place folded cloths and bandages on top of them, and bind those with a bandage that is made in this way:
And then take two cloths and soak them with alum-dyed wool in this manner; make the ends of those cloths that are pressed with string or damp wool, and attach them to the underwear, and one end should be attached to the buttocks between the legs, and the second end should be attached to the area near the pubic bone, and two ends on each side over the thighs and two other ends on each side of the hips; and all the bandage should be tightened in the underwear.
And sometimes this hernia is treated artificially with cauterization instead of incision with iron; and it involves taking a thin knife-like cautery tool and making an incision in the groin of the genitals, then igniting it as we have recommended until the white membrane containing the water is exposed. And then take cautery in this way: And it is shaped like the Greek letter "gamma". (Γ)
And then puncture the white membrane with it and ignite until all the fluid is removed.
And then extend the white membrane with forceps and remove it with forceps, and use a fine cautery tool to remove it as well; cut the white membrane as much as possible until you uproot all of it; be careful that the fire does not touch the water sac.
And know that this operation is safer and less prone to bleeding than an incision-based operation.
But if an abscess forms during the incision or during cauterization or bleeding occurs, then you must treat it as necessary based on what has happened, according to what has been said.
But if the patient is weak and does not hope for a second operation due to its horror, then administer puncture as we have recommended; this is when you are certain, based on what has been said about the signs, that the hernia contains water.
Then it is necessary to place the patient on an elevated cushion, puncture the abscess in its lowest part with a broad spatula and continue the incision according to the length of the body.
And make the opening wide enough so that all the fluid flows out.
And then place a cloth over it and bind it, leaving it alone so that the remaining fluid flows out. And take care of it until the wound is healed.
But if there is an obstacle to the removal of the fluid during that time, then you must puncture again; this should not be done unless the white membrane in the opening of the wound is preventing the flow of fluid. In that case, insert a probe or instrument used for extracting water from hydrops into the wound, or place a small piece of cloth on the pressure point of the wound.
And know that the fluid may return and accumulate again over several months or years; when this happens, it should be treated in the same way, for the patient will also endure his days this way.

On incision for soft tissue hernia and its treatment.
And know that in the incision for this type of hernia, there is fear of danger to life, especially in severe cases; therefore, I recommend dismissal and preservation of life with the best option available. (Note: This seems to suggest avoiding surgery in high-risk cases)

And a dark-colored abscess called "lapificated" is usually not painful and cannot be felt. (Note: It seems like the text is describing another type of abscess)
And sometimes abscesses are caused by knots in the arteries and can be felt due to their swelling, or by inflammation of veins. Chapter 64.
Of the treatment of hernia which is of the belly (abdomen).
The belly (abdomen) is an abscess enclosed in some kind of covering similar to a hernia with swelling of the testicles, and it causes difficult movement and walking for the patient.
And in the treatment of this illness, it is done with caution due to what precedes it: fear.
However, we must say operation in the second case following what was done in the first.

Then make an incision with a broad, sharp spatula for transverse section into the vessels until they are exposed.
Then scrape all around, just as we have said in the extraction of hernia in the temples.
Then place a needle in there with double thread, and tie it at the first location where the hernia occurs, and then tie another knot at the end of the thread. Then take care of the wound with treatment for other wounds in which you want health to be generated so that the vessels fall which do not nourish one of the two testicles, because it is not harmful.
But if the hernia occurs in all of the vessels, then it is necessary to extract the testicles or that the testicles become atrophied due to the absence of nourishment from the vessels that have been cut, leading to their removal, or that they are damaged to such an extent that they cannot be helpful.
Chapter 65.
Of the treatment of internal hernia.
The occurrence of this hernia is due to a tear in the membrane covering the abdomen that extends from the navel towards the side of the belly, causing intestines to protrude through the rupture.
And this rupture can be either in the membrane itself or from its deficiency, and it occurs for many reasons: violent blows, jumps, loud noises, heavy lifting, or similar causes.
And the sign of this is when it occurs gradually over a long period of time due to extension of the membrane, and not suddenly, and it forms a swelling like an abscess near the navel because the membrane compresses the intestines.
And the sign of this is when it occurs due to tearing of the membrane, as at the beginning it causes violent pain suddenly; and it forms an abscess that appears different from the one near the navel, and this is due to protrusion of the intestine, and the body of the hernia is located outside the membrane.
And sometimes part of the intestine protrudes through the membrane along with the hernia sac, and this type is called an internal hernia or "zirbal".
And sometimes the hernia is caused by gas, and in some cases it runs along the intestinal fold and becomes trapped there, leading to serious complications for the patient; and in some cases it causes severe pain that worsens when pressed.
And in the treatment of this type of illness with iron, caution is required because it is important to avoid any injury or damage to the surrounding tissues.
And the method of operating on this type of illness is to instruct the patient to push back the intestine using their own hand towards the inside of their cavity if they are able to do so; and then have them lie on their stomach between your hands, while you raise their legs.
Then pull the string that ties the scrotum to the abdomen upwards, and make an incision along the entire length of the scrotal cord; and then insert two hooks into the edges of the incision to hold it open as needed.
And if the incision is made to the extent that is necessary and safe, allowing the testicle to be released from the hernia sac.
Then scrape away any excess tissue below the scrotal cord until the white, hard fascia of the abdominal wall is visible from all sides.
Then insert your finger into the incision where the testicle is located, between the white fascia and the scrotal cord, and gently separate any adhesions found in the area behind the testicle.
Then use your hand to gently pull the scrotal cord away from the incision, extending the white fascial layer with your left hand while lifting the testicle and surrounding tissue up towards the incision using your right hand. Instruct an assistant to carefully stretch the testicle towards the incision while you use a medical solution to dissolve any remaining adhesions present in the area behind the testicle.
And ensure with your hands that there is no part of the intestine trapped within the hard, white fascial layer. But if you find any part of it (the intestine) trapped there, then gently push it back down towards the abdomen.
Then make an incision in the area below the scrotal cord, allowing blood and pus to flow out as described earlier in the text.
Then apply wool soaked in oil to the wound and cover it; administer the recommended treatment (and in some cases, cauterize the white fascial layer, which we mentioned earlier may cause bleeding during incision due to its vascular nature) and leave the dressing in place until it falls off naturally.
But if the wound takes a long time to heal, then apply warm water with a rag and place it over the wound until it falls off naturally.
Then take care of the wound with other treatments until it is healed.
Chapter 66
On Hernia Ventosa (Ventral Hernia)
In this hernia, I have not seen anyone who has been daring enough to attempt its cure with iron (a cautery).
And the first (doctors) said that it should be done as we have recommended for the hernia that is open; which is to tie off the blood vessels near the incision site with ease, and then cauterize the area in the middle where the abscess is located with the substance that causes it to subside, until the vessels fall away.
And cure the wound as we have said until it is healed.
Chapter 67.
On the disruption (dislocation) that occurs in the joints.
Sometimes, however, a disruption (dislocation) in the joints occurs as we have said, and it protrudes (emerges).
And the testicles should not be given any cause by the intestines; and if they are, it is only a little; and it returns in all cases.
But if the duration of time with this is prolonged, then a fissure forms in the abdomen where the intestines descend into the abdomen; and this happens due to the extension of the abdomen, which occurs in the joints as we have said. The cause of this is that the abdomen is stretched out, and it becomes softened, and the location is infected and protruding.
And the cure for it is with a cautery, just as was described in its narrative.
And sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies on their back with their legs between your hands, and you dry the location of the disruption or protruding abscess with a section three finger-widths wide.
And then strengthen the white abdomen that is under the collarbone until it is exposed.
And then take the rod (or "ray") and place it over the protruding location on the abdomen, and press it against the pressure point of the belly.
And then bring the two protruding locations on the end of the rod (or "ray") of the abdomen together, and join them with a stitch (or "suture").
And then withdraw the end of the rod (or "ray"), and do not cut deeply into the abdomen, nor extend the incision too much, nor cause any other harm as you know in the treatment of intestinal hernias.
And then cure that with the treatment of wounds (or "plaguas"), and when you make incisions in the fields (or "fiels"), clean that area and restore the wound until it is consolidated, because the abdomen (or "ciphac") is constricted and the protrusion (or "eminencia de ruptura") is not adjusted.
And cautery is more effective in this case, because it is closer to a cure.
Chapter 68. (Note: In medieval texts, chapters were often referred to by their number in Roman numerals)
On the softening of the spermatic cord.
Often in older men, the spermatic cord is softened because the flesh that surrounds it has become soft, and this requires careful observation. (Note: "Aysso" is a Middle Age term used to refer to something similar or identical to what was mentioned before)
Therefore, it is necessary for the caregiver in charge of treating this condition to have the patient lie on their back and lift the softened cord up onto the natural cord, then secure both with a stitch.
And if desired, cut off the excess of the softened cord at the beginning with three or four sutures and firm stitching. (Note: "Cus" here refers to cutting, probably with scissors)
Then stitch between the sutures; and take care to heal any other wounds in the area before it heals and pus forms.
Chapter 69. (Note: In medieval texts, chapters were often referred to by their number in Roman numerals)
On Castration.
Know that castration is forbidden in our religion, but it is necessary for me to mention it in this book; and its mention is only required in two circumstances: firstly, so that the doctor knows the treatment when asked about it, and secondly because we often need to castrate other animals for our livestock such as horses, pigs, and similar animals. (Note: The word "castratio" here refers to surgical removal of the testicles)
And so I say that castration is done in two ways: either by constriction or by incision and sectioning. (Note: "Attrissio" here likely refers to twisting off the spermatic cord, while "fissura a seccio" means making an incision and cutting through the tissue)
But in the case of castration by constriction, the method of the operation is to submerge the animal in hot water until its genitals become soft and limp. On the shape of the instruments that are used for cauterization.
Sometimes cauterization is done with instruments made of silver or lead or melted iron, hammered; and sometimes it is done with instruments that are small or large, according to the patient's needs, because the instrument used for curing small children should be small; and those with blunt or rounded tips, the cauteries for those should be small.

The end of the cannula above where the bag is attached should be wide in this manner, and it should have a distinct mark where the bag is attached, as shown here.
And the end of the probe that is inserted in the hole should be blunt (that is, not sharp) and gradually tapering to a point; and on one side of it there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole, and the diameter of the holes should correspond to the thickness of the veins and slightly larger.
And the bag in which the medications (made from animal bladder or sheep's wool) are placed should be the size of a hand-span.
And it should be pierced with multiple holes, as many as the rotation allows, and the space between the holes should correspond to the width of a finger.
And insert in these holes a strong cord of raw gall that is made from ten galls, or wrap it around them; and attach the bag to this. And when the bag is placed on the area to be cauterized, it should be tightly secured at the end of the probe with strong compression, and then cauterize through each hole: However, the method for cauterizing with each hole is that you fill the bag with the medication, which should be warmed according to the patient's tolerance; and make sure it is not too hot or too cold.
Then have the patient lie down on their back, raise their legs and place a cushion under them, and place a hot water bottle or a heating pad over them.
